Eight\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:G8_organization.svg" class="image" title="Map of G8 member nations and the European Union"><img alt="Map of title="Japan">Japan</a></b>\n</p><p><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" href="#cite_note-russia-suspension-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></b>\n</p><p><b><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a></b>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>G8</b>, reformatted as <b><a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a></b> from 2014 due to the suspension of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>\'s participation,<sup id="cite_ref-russia-suspension_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russia-suspension-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> was an inter-governmental political forum from 1997 until 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-cfr_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfr-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The forum originated with a <a href="/wiki/1st_G6_summit" title="1st G6 summit">1975 summit</a> hosted by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> that brought together representatives of six governments: France, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, thus leading to the name <b>Group of Six</b> or <b>G6</b>. The summit came to be known as the <b>Group of Seven</b>, or <b>G7</b>, in 1976 with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> was added to the political forum from 1997, which the following year became known as the G8. In March 2014 Russia was suspended \nindefinitely following the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a>, whereupon the political forum name reverted to G7.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 Russia announced its permanent withdrawal from the G8<sup id="cite_ref-russia-suspension_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russia-suspension-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>. However, several representatives of G7 countries stated that they would be interested in Russia\'s return to the group.<sup id="cite_ref-TASS_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TASS-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ANSA_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANSA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ischinger_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ischinger-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinmeier_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steinmeier-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abe_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abe-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alfano_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alfano-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lindner_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindner-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bundestag_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundestag-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wagenknecht_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wagenknecht-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trump_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trump-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> was represented at the G8 since the 1980s as a "nonenumerated" participant, but originally could not host or chair summits.<sup id="cite_ref-EU_info_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_info-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/40th_G7_summit" title="40th G7 summit">40th summit</a> was the first time the European Union was able to host and chair a summit.\nCollectively, in 2012 the G8 nations comprised <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">50.1 percent of 2012 global nominal GDP</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">40.9 percent of global GDP (PPP)</a>.\n</p><p>"G7" can refer to the member states in aggregate or to the annual <a href="/wiki/Summit_meeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Summit meeting">summit meeting</a> of the G7 <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of government">heads of government</a>. G7 ministers also meet throughout the year, such as the <a href="/wiki/G7_(finance_ministers)" class="mw-redirect" title="G7 (finance ministers)">G7 finance ministers</a> (who meet four times a year), G7 foreign ministers, or G7 environment ministers.\n</p><p>Each calendar year, the responsibility of hosting the G8 was rotated through the member states in the following order: France, United States, United Kingdom, Russia (suspended), Germany, Japan, Italy, and Canada. The holder of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency" title="Presidency">presidency</a> sets the agenda, hosts the summit for that year, and determines which ministerial meetings will take place.\n</p><p>In 2005, the UK government initiated the practice of inviting five leading emerging markets \xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> \xe2\x80\x94 to participate in the G8 meetings that came to be known as <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a>, but this practice was short-lived.<sup id="cite_ref-cfr_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfr-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20 major economies</a> growing in stature since the <a href="/wiki/2008_G-20_Washington_summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 G-20 Washington summit">2008 Washington summit</a>, world leaders from the group announced at their <a href="/wiki/2009_G-20_Pittsburgh_summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 G-20 Pittsburgh summit">Pittsburgh summit</a> in September 2009 that the group would replace the G8 as the main economic council of wealthy nations.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, the G7 retains its relevance as a "steering group for the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-cfr_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfr-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> with special significance appointed to Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="toctext">Relevance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Youth_8_Summit"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Youth 8 Summit</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven#History" title="Group of Seven">Group of Seven \xc2\xa7&#160;History</a></div>\n<p>Following <a href="/wiki/20th_G7_summit" title="20th G7 summit">1994\'s G7 summit in Naples</a>, Russian officials held separate meetings with leaders of the G7 after the group\'s summits. This informal arrangement was dubbed the Political 8 (P8)\xe2\x80\x94or, colloquially, the G7+1. At the invitation of UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> was invited first as a guest observer, later as a full participant. It was seen as a way to encourage Yeltsin with his capitalist reforms. Russia formally joined the group in 1998, resulting in the Group of Eight, or G8.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(July 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>A major focus of the G8 since 2009 has been the global <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">supply of food</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_5May_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_5May-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> At the 2009 <a href="/wiki/L%27Aquila" title="L&#39;Aquila">L\'Aquila</a> summit, the G8\'s members promised to contribute $22 billion to the issue. By 2015, 93% of funds had been disbursed.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Chicago_Council_on_Global_Affairs_15Mar_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Chicago_Council_on_Global_Affairs_15Mar-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the 2012 summit, President Barack Obama asked G8 leaders to adopt the New Alliance for Food Security and Nutrition initiative to "help the rural poor produce more food and sell it in thriving local and regional markets as well as on the global market".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Russia.E2.80.B2s_participation_suspension_.282014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia\xe2\x80\xb2s_participation_suspension_(2014)">Russia\xe2\x80\xb2s participation suspension (2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Russia\xe2\x80\xb2s participation suspension (2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 24 March 2014, the G7 members cancelled the planned <a href="/wiki/40th_G7_summit" title="40th G7 summit">G8 summit</a> that was to be held in June that year in the Russian city of Sochi, and suspended Russia\xe2\x80\xb2s membership of the group, due to <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Russia\'s annexation of Crimea</a>; nevertheless, they stopped short of outright permanent expulsion.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Russian foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Lavrov" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergei Lavrov">Sergei Lavrov</a> downplayed the importance of the decision by the U.S. and its allies, and pointed up that major international decisions were taken by the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Insider_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insider-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later on, the Italian Foreign Affairs minister <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a> and other Italian authorities,<sup id="cite_ref-TASS_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TASS-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ANSA_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ANSA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> along with the <a href="/wiki/EastWest_Institute" title="EastWest Institute">EastWest Institute</a> board member <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Ischinger" title="Wolfgang Ischinger">Wolfgang Ischinger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ischinger_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ischinger-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> suggested that Russia may restore its membership in the group. In April 2015, the German foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier" title="Frank-Walter Steinmeier">Frank-Walter Steinmeier</a> said that Russia would be welcomed to return to G8 provided the <a href="/wiki/Minsk_Protocol" title="Minsk Protocol">Minsk Protocol</a> was implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-Steinmeier_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steinmeier-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, he added that "none of the major international conflicts can be solved without Russia", and the G7 countries will consider Russia\'s return to the group in 2017. The same year, Japanese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" title="Shinz\xc5\x8d Abe">Shinz\xc5\x8d Abe</a> called for Russia\'s return to G8, stating that Russia\'s involvement is "crucial to tackling multiple crises in the Middle East".<sup id="cite_ref-Abe_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abe-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, the Italian foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Angelino_Alfano" title="Angelino Alfano">Angelino Alfano</a> said that Italy hopes for "resuming the G8 format with Russia and ending the atmosphere of the Cold War".<sup id="cite_ref-Alfano_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alfano-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> On 13 January 2017, Russia announced that it would permanently leave the G8 grouping.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Lindner" title="Christian Lindner">Christian Lindner</a>, the leader of <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Democratic Party of Germany">Free Democratic Party of Germany</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a>, said that Putin should be "asked to join the table of the G7" so that one could "talk with him and not about him", and "we cannot make all things dependent on the situation in Crimea".<sup id="cite_ref-Lindner_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindner-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, the German politicians and members of the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a> <a href="/wiki/Sahra_Wagenknecht" title="Sahra Wagenknecht">Sahra Wagenknecht</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graf_Lambsdorff" title="Alexander Graf Lambsdorff">Alexander Graf Lambsdorff</a> said that Russia should be invited back to the group and attend the <a href="/wiki/44th_G7_summit" title="44th G7 summit">2018 summit in Canada</a>: "Russia should again be at the table during the [June] summit at the latest" because "peace in Europe and also in the Middle East is only possible with Russia".<sup id="cite_ref-Bundestag_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundestag-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wagenknecht_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wagenknecht-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The President of US <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> also stated that Russia should be returned to G8; his appeal was supported by the Italian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Conte" title="Giuseppe Conte">Giuseppe Conte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Trump_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trump-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>Later the 4 EU members of G7, Canada and Japan anyway didn\'t agree about it.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> After several G7 members quickly rejected US President Trump suggestion to accept again Russian Federation in the G8, Russian Foreign Minister Lavrov said Russian Federation isn\'t interested to rejoin the political forum G8. He also said that G20 is sufficient for Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In the final statement of 2018 Canada meeting, the G7 members announced to recall sanctions and also to be ready to take further restrictive measures against the Russian Federation for the failure of Minsk Agreement complete implementation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_and_activities">Structure and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structure and activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg/240px-Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg" width="240" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg/360px-Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg/480px-Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ten_leaders_at_G8_summit,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaders of the G8 on 18 June 2013, in <a href="/wiki/Lough_Erne" title="Lough Erne">Lough Erne</a>, Northern Ireland, United Kingdom</div></div></div>\n<p>By design, the G8 deliberately lacked an administrative structure like those for international organizations, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> or the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>. The group does not have a permanent secretariat, or offices for its members.\n</p><p>The presidency of the group rotates annually among member countries, with each new term beginning on 1 January of the year. The rotation order is: France, the United States, the United Kingdom, Russia (suspended), Germany, Japan, Italy, and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The country holding the presidency is responsible for planning and hosting a series of ministerial-level meetings, leading up to a mid-year summit attended by the heads of government. The president of the European Commission participates as an equal in all summit events.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ministerial meetings bring together ministers responsible for various portfolios to discuss issues of mutual or global concern. The range of topics include health, law enforcement, labor, economic and social development, energy, environment, foreign affairs, justice and interior, terrorism, and trade. There are also a separate set of meetings known as the <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a>, created during the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Gleneagles,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Gleneagles, Scotland">Gleneagles</a>, Scotland summit, that is attended by finance and energy ministers from all eight member countries in addition to the five "outreach countries" which are also known as the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Five" title="Group of Five">Group of Five</a>\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2005, justice ministers and interior ministers from the G8 countries agreed to launch an international database on <a href="/wiki/Pedophile" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedophile">pedophiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pedophile_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pedophile-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The G8 officials also agreed to pool data on <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>, subject to restrictions by privacy and security laws in individual countries.<sup id="cite_ref-terrorismdata_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terrorismdata-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_energy">Global energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Global energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/International_Partnership_for_Energy_Efficiency_Cooperation" title="International Partnership for Energy Efficiency Cooperation">International Partnership for Energy Efficiency Cooperation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_Investment_Funds" title="Climate Investment Funds">Climate Investment Funds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg/240px-G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg/360px-G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg/480px-G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G8_leaders_confer_together.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>G8 leaders confer during the <a href="/wiki/35th_G8_summit" title="35th G8 summit">2009 summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/L%27Aquila" title="L&#39;Aquila">L\'Aquila</a> (<a href="/wiki/Abruzzo" title="Abruzzo">Abruzzo</a>, Italy).</div></div></div>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/33rd_G8_summit" title="33rd G8 summit">Heiligendamm Summit</a> in 2007, the G8 acknowledged a proposal from the EU for a worldwide initiative on <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">efficient energy use</a>. They agreed to explore, along with the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>, the most effective means to promote energy efficiency internationally. A year later, on 8 June 2008, the G8 along with China, India, South Korea and the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a> established the <a href="/wiki/International_Partnership_for_Energy_Efficiency_Cooperation" title="International Partnership for Energy Efficiency Cooperation">International Partnership for Energy Efficiency Cooperation</a>, at the Energy Ministerial meeting hosted by Japan holding 2008 G8 Presidency, in <a href="/wiki/Aomori,_Aomori" class="mw-redirect" title="Aomori, Aomori">Aomori</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>G8 Finance Ministers, whilst in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/34th_G8_summit" title="34th G8 summit">34th Summit of the G8 Heads of State and Government</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toyako,_Hokkaido" class="mw-redirect" title="Toyako, Hokkaido">Toyako, Hokkaido</a>, met on the 13 and 14 June 2008, in <a href="/wiki/Osaka,_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Osaka, Japan">Osaka, Japan</a>. They agreed to the "G8 Action Plan for Climate Change to Enhance the Engagement of Private and Public Financial Institutions." In closing, Ministers supported the launch of new <a href="/wiki/Climate_Investment_Funds" title="Climate Investment Funds">Climate Investment Funds</a> (CIFs) by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, which will help existing efforts until a new framework under the <a href="/wiki/UNFCCC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFCCC">UNFCCC</a> is implemented after 2012. The UNFCCC is not on track to meeting any of its stated goals.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_summit">Annual summit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Annual summit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven#List_of_summits" title="Group of Seven">Group of Seven \xc2\xa7&#160;List of summits</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/23rd_G8_summit" title="23rd G8 summit">first G8 summit</a> was held in 1997 after Russia formally joined the G7 group, and the <a href="/wiki/39th_G8_summit" title="39th G8 summit">last one</a> was held in 2013. The <a href="/wiki/40th_G7_summit" title="40th G7 summit">2014 summit</a> was scheduled to be held in Russia. However, due to the <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Crimean crisis">Crimean crisis</a>, the other seven countries decided to hold a separate meeting without Russia as a G7 summit in Brussels, Belgium.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg/220px-36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg/330px-36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg/440px-36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2690" data-file-height="1424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:36th_G8_summit_member_cropped_36th_G8_summit_member_20100625.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The G8 leaders at the <a href="/wiki/36th_G8_summit" title="36th G8 summit">36th summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Ontario" title="Huntsville, Ontario">Huntsville, Ontario</a>. Left to right: <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Van Rompuy</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>), <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Harper" title="Stephen Harper">Harper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Medvedev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naoto_Kan" title="Naoto Kan">Kan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Berlusconi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jose_Manuel_Barroso" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Manuel Barroso">Barroso</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>), <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Merkel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Sarkozy</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg/280px-Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg" width="280" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg/420px-Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg/560px-Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Genova-G8_2001-Incidenti_a_Corso_Torino.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>20 July 2001, <a href="/wiki/27th_G8_summit" title="27th G8 summit">27th G8 summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, Italy: Protesters burn a police vehicle</div></div></div>\n<p>Some criticism centres on the assertion that members of G8 do not do enough to help global problems, due to strict <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a> policy and other issues related to <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">globalization</a>. In <i>Unraveling Global Apartheid</i>, political analyst Titus Alexander described the G7, as it was in 1996, as the \'cabinet\' of global minority rule, with a coordinating role in world affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">Heritage Foundation</a> has criticized the G8 for advocating food security without making room for economic freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-HF17May_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HF17May-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relevance">Relevance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Relevance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The G8\'s relevance has been subject to debate from 2008 onward.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It represented the major <a href="/wiki/Industrialized_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialized countries">industrialized countries</a> but critics argued that the G8 no longer represented the world\'s most powerful economies, as China <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">has surpassed</a> every economy but the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vladimir Putin did not attend the 2012 G8 summit at Camp David, causing <i><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy" title="Foreign Policy">Foreign Policy</a></i> (<i>FP</i>) magazine to remark that the summit has generally outlived its usefulness as a viable international gathering of foreign leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-FN_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FN-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Two years later, Russia was suspended from the G8, then chose to leave permanently in January 2017.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> major economies leaders\' summit has had an increased level of international prestige and influence.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> said of the G8 in 2012:<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>Some people ask, does the G8 still matter, when we have a Group of 20? My answer is, yes. The G8 is a group of like-minded countries that share a belief in free enterprise as the best route to growth. As eight countries making up about half the world\'s gross domestic product, the standards we set, the commitments we make, and the steps we take can help solve vital global issues, fire up economies and drive prosperity all over the world.</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_8_Summit">Youth 8 Summit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_of_Eight&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Youth 8 Summit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Y8 Summit or simply Y8, formerly known as the G8 Youth Summit<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> is the youth counterpart to the G8 summit.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The summits were organized from 2006 to 2013. The first summit to use the name Y8 took place in May 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, alongside the Youth G8 that took place in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> the same year. From 2016 onwards, similar youth conferences were organized under the name Y7 Summit.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Y8 Summit brings together young leaders from G8 nations and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> to facilitate discussions of <a href="/wiki/International_affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="International affairs">international affairs</a>, promote cross-cultural understanding, and build global friendships. The conference closely follows the formal negotiation procedures of the G8 Summit.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Y8 Summit represents the innovative voice of young adults between the age of 18 and 35. At the end of the summit, the delegates jointly come up with a consensus-based<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> written statement, the Final Communiqu\xc3\xa9.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> This document is subsequently presented to G8 leaders in order to inspire positive change.\n</p><p>The Y8 Summit was organized annually by a global network of youth-led organizations called The IDEA (The International Diplomatic Engagement Association).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The organizations undertake the selection processes for their respective national delegations, while the hosting country is responsible for organizing the summit. An example of such a youth-led organization is the <a href="/wiki/Young_European_Leadership" title="Young European Leadership">Young European Leadership</a> association, which recruits and sends EU Delegates.\n</p><p>The goal of the Y8 Summit is to bring together young people from around the world to allow the voices and opinions of young generations to be heard and to encourage them to take part in global decision-making processes.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:85%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th></th>\n<th style="width:45%">Summit</th>\n<th style="width:15%">Year</th>\n<th
